INDEX
A NOTE TO THE USER

Persona Names. The user of this index should be as imaginative in his pursuit of a surname
as a colonial clerk might have been in his spelling. Virtually all variant spellings of personal
names in the abstracts are unchanged in the index. The indexers have not presumed to
decide, for example, whether the Jno. Abbott mentioned on page 2 is the same person as
the John Abett mentioned on page 51. Most civilian and military titles have been omitted
from the index when both the given name and title are present in the abstracts. Thus,
under the entry Addams the page number for the subentry Mr. indicates that no given
name appears in the abstract (or in the patent book). In such cases the user is allowed to
decide for himself whether the Mr. Addams mentioned in a 1725 patent on page 292 may
be one of the persons named under the entry Adams, or Addams, or Addam. Dashes are
used in place of given names (e.g., Aldridge, ———, 82, 318) or surnames (e.g.,
Alice ———,, 1) if information was missing or illegible in the patent.

Piace-NAMEs. Minor variant spellings of place-names and variant abbreviations of geo-
graphical terms have not been retained in the index; for example, the subject entry
Counties, Accomack, does not reflect other variant spellings that may appear in the
abstracts. Again, the user should remember that colonial clerks were recording many names
for which there were no standard English spellings, and that the index consolidates only
the obvious variant spellings of place-names. No attempt is made to indicate the best or
most frequent spellings of place-names used during the colonial period.

Susyecr Heapines. Researchers will find entries for these major subject categories under
the following headings that appear in the index in capital letters:
